  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_4c5177c4-43ae-4f41-b92a-2a5ca9fc9d8c'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

    <a title="Kyle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9740056-kyle"><img alt="Kyle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481754383p2/9740056.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1156090221?book_show_action=true">Jan 04, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kyle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kyle" href="/user/show/9740056-kyle">Kyle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780316025690" href="/book/show/7073921-hunters-of-the-dusk">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1156090221" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9099301592836452603"><div>
  <p>Another adventure off to a good start.</p>
  <p>Prince Darren, along with Larten Crepsley and Harkat Mulds, are sent off on a special mission to hunt the Vampaneze Lord by Mr. Tiny.</p>
  <p>I really enjoy Darren as a main character. It will be interesting to see where the other takes things as the story progresses. As with the other stories in the series, the book is well written, and has no ending. I'll have to read the next book in the series to continue the plot started in this book. Which is one of my</p></div></span>
  <span id="freeText9099301592836452603" style="display:none"><div>
  <p>Another adventure off to a good start.</p>
  <p>Prince Darren, along with Larten Crepsley and Harkat Mulds, are sent off on a special mission to hunt the Vampaneze Lord by Mr. Tiny.</p>
  <p>I really enjoy Darren as a main character. It will be interesting to see where the other takes things as the story progresses. As with the other stories in the series, the book is well written, and has no ending. I'll have to read the next book in the series to continue the plot started in this book. Which is one of my biggest annoyances about this series. Why three 200 page books rather than one 600 page book?</p>
  <p>It's so hard to rate a book when it's not finished. Did I like what I've read so far? Sure it was engaging and I want to pick up the next book so i can see what happens next. But I really shouldn't have to. I should be able to just turn the page and start the next chapter.</p>
  <p>To read my review of the other books in this series, use the links below:</p>
  <blockquote>
      Book One: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1156090036" rel="nofollow noopener">A Living Nightmare</a> <br />	 Book Two: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1156090062" rel="nofollow noopener">The Vampire's Assistant</a> <br />	 Book Three: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1156090092" rel="nofollow noopener">Tunnels of Blood</a> <br />	 Book Four: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1156090131" rel="nofollow noopener">Vampire Mountain</a> <br />	 Book Five: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1671698784" rel="nofollow noopener">Trials of Death</a> <br />	 Book Six: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1559712336" rel="nofollow noopener">The Vampire Prince</a>  
  </blockquote>
  <br />

<div id="review_2944703594" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2944703594" />
    <a title="Rosaline (Rosaline&#39;s Rolls &amp; Scrolls)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23822042-rosaline-rosaline-s-rolls-scrolls"><img alt="Rosaline (Rosaline&#39;s Rolls &amp; Scrolls)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1581593489p2/23822042.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2944703594?book_show_action=true">Aug 20, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rosaline (Rosaline&#39;s Rolls &amp; Scrolls)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rosaline (Rosaline&#39;s Rolls &amp; Scrolls)" href="/user/show/23822042-rosaline-rosaline-s-rolls-scrolls">Rosaline (Rosaline&#39;s Rolls &amp; Scrolls)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23822042-rosaline-rosaline-s-rolls-scrolls?shelf=2-and-a-half-stars">2-and-a-half-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23822042-rosaline-rosaline-s-rolls-scrolls?shelf=did-not-like-the-hero">did-not-like-the-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23822042-rosaline-rosaline-s-rolls-scrolls?shelf=first-person-narrative">first-person-narrative</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23822042-rosaline-rosaline-s-rolls-scrolls?shelf=read-in-2019">read-in-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23822042-rosaline-rosaline-s-rolls-scrolls?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23822042-rosaline-rosaline-s-rolls-scrolls?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23822042-rosaline-rosaline-s-rolls-scrolls?shelf=the-floor-is-lava-challenge-2019">the-floor-is-lava-challenge-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23822042-rosaline-rosaline-s-rolls-scrolls?shelf=i-have-predictions">i-have-predictions</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23822042-rosaline-rosaline-s-rolls-scrolls?shelf=in-series">in-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23822042-rosaline-rosaline-s-rolls-scrolls?shelf=reread">reread</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2944703594" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1719550216599089089"><b>Reread: Aug-20-2019 <br/>Actual rating: 2.5 Stars<br/></b><br/>I did not really care about this book. I first read it so long ago that I felt like I was reading the book for the first time. But this time I didn't enjoy it much. Gone was the excitement and wonder of youth and I found myself bored instead. <br/><br/>I did not like the writing at all. The book read like the first draft of half a story. I felt like it was written in a day or two. And nothing really got concluded in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8963.Hunters_of_the_Dusk__Cirque_Du_Freak___7_' title='Hunters of the Dusk (Cirque Du Freak, #7) by Darren Shan' rel='nofollow noopener'>Hunters of the Dusk</a> as is the way of Darren Sh</span>
  <span id="freeText1719550216599089089" style="display:none"><b>Reread: Aug-20-2019 <br>Actual rating: 2.5 Stars<br></b><br>I did not really care about this book. I first read it so long ago that I felt like I was reading the book for the first time. But this time I didn't enjoy it much. Gone was the excitement and wonder of youth and I found myself bored instead. <br><br>I did not like the writing at all. The book read like the first draft of half a story. I felt like it was written in a day or two. And nothing really got concluded in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8963.Hunters_of_the_Dusk__Cirque_Du_Freak___7_" title="Hunters of the Dusk (Cirque Du Freak, #7) by Darren Shan" rel="nofollow noopener">Hunters of the Dusk</a> as is the way of Darren Shan's books. They all feel like part of a bigger novel instead of separate novels in a series. <br><br>I did not like the main character, Darren. I saw no developments on his part and for me he has lost all personality.<br><br>All the other characters, especially the supposedly big and powerful vampires were like adult characters in children's cartoons. They had weird logic and just were so indecisive and overall unnecessary.<br><br>I, however, did not absolutely hate the book either. It was okay for what it was. Though I'm not sure what it was. For me Cirque Du Freak was good when I was a kid. Now it's just a sloppy excuse for a series. <br><br>Also, the "mysteries" are so obvious. They should reveal them already!<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1462932760ra/19062151.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="1719550216599089089" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_279611547" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/279611547" />
    <a title="Whitney" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4881155-whitney"><img alt="Whitney" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1439004129p2/4881155.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/279611547?book_show_action=true">Feb 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Whitney" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Whitney" href="/user/show/4881155-whitney">Whitney</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4881155-whitney?shelf=supernatural">supernatural</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4881155-whitney?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4881155-whitney?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4881155-whitney?shelf=two-stars">two-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4881155-whitney?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4881155-whitney?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer279611547" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15598067620930459636">Six years have passed since <i>The Vampire Prince</i> and the vampires are at war with the vampaneze. Along comes Mr. Tiny, bearing an ominous look into the future. Darren, Mr. Crepsley, and Harkat Mulds are dispatched on a mission to do the impossible; find and kill the Lord of the vampaneze. If they should fail, the destruction of the vampire world will be on their hands.<br/><br/><b>Plot</b><br/><br/>Though I found the overall plot of <i>Hunters of the Dusk</i> boring, I’m glad I didn’t have to sit through the six years that Darren </span>
  <span id="freeText15598067620930459636" style="display:none">Six years have passed since <i>The Vampire Prince</i> and the vampires are at war with the vampaneze. Along comes Mr. Tiny, bearing an ominous look into the future. Darren, Mr. Crepsley, and Harkat Mulds are dispatched on a mission to do the impossible; find and kill the Lord of the vampaneze. If they should fail, the destruction of the vampire world will be on their hands.<br /><br /><b>Plot</b><br /><br />Though I found the overall plot of <i>Hunters of the Dusk</i> boring, I’m glad I didn’t have to sit through the six years that Darren was stuck inside of Vampire Mountain. The short amount of time with Darren inside Vampire Mountain in <i>The Vampire Prince</i> was more than enough, six years honestly might have killed me. And it’s sad to say, the plot in this book was boring as the last one and didn’t pick up until the very end. The same thing happened in <i>The Vampire Prince</i>; the majority of the book is about preparing for something and the last part is action packed. I wasn’t as enthused to read this book since it has a same sort of feeling as <i>The Vampire Prince</i>. At the very least, the story is finally, <i>finally</i> moving forward. It’s taken many set up books but at least the end is in the horizon.<br /><br />In <i>Hunters of the Dark</i>, after a six year time skip, Darren and the vampires are at war with the vampaneze. Mr. Tiny shows up and really gets the ball moving. This is good, but it feels forced. And then Darren &amp; Co. go out into the world to search for the Vampaneze Lord. The majority of the book is just them travelling around; that’s where the boring part comes from.<br /><br /><b>Writing</b><br /><br />The writing was lackluster. If a writer <i>has</i> to include things into their book that isn’t very thrilling, they need to be able to make it exiting anyways. I’ve said before in and earlier review of one of the books in this series that Shan doesn’t do this particularly well. Usually he just skips over these parts, but when he can’t and has to write them, the reader suffers. His writing is still good, I’d probably never say it wasn’t, but when he’s not introducing new things or writing action scenes, Shan’s writing isn’t very engaging. <br /><br /><b>Characters</b><br /><br />I feel very odd about Darren. He’s mentally around twenty-five, I believe, yet he still thinks rather foolishly. The scene where he’s going through the Purge is the best example I’ve seen. He’s actually talking to his reflection like a toddler; not like a child but more like a baby. I don’t know if Shan wrote that part for laughs or what but it wasn’t all that funny. We know Darren is smarter than that so I don’t know why that scene was dragged out for more than a second where Darren should have been startled at first but then quickly realized that it was his reflection.<br /><br />We have two reoccurring characters: Mr. Crepsley and Harkat Mulds. Even though Darren is supposed to have a close relationship with the two of them, once again, it’s not really shown. It’s not like Shan doesn’t know how to write friendships, he did it easily with Darren’s friendship between Steve, Evra, and Sam. I guess because they are more adult characters.<br /><br />And we meet a new main character, the missing Prince Vancha March. The first few chapters with Vancha made me not really like him. He was obnoxious and it feels like his personality was played up too much. I can see the potential in him and liked him a bit close to the end of the book.<br /><br /><b>Things I Didn't Like</b><br /><br />My biggest problem with <i>Hunters of the Dusk</i> was how boring it was. It was just dull. I hope the action picks up again the next book, because it’ll be difficult going through five more books like this. There’s not much more to say about that.<br /><br />The other problem I had with the book was how I noticed the female characters are treated. There are six women total in the <i>Cirque du Freak</i> series thus far that have at least one line of dialogue and names. They are Mrs. Shan, Mrs. Leonard, Mrs. Hemlock, Debbie, Arra Sails, and Evanna (who is introduced in this book). The first three women have no other roles except to be mothers for a short period of time. Debbie and Arra Sails are both love interests, Arra of which who is killed to incite man-pain in Mr. Crepsley. Evanna, we are told, was created so that vampires could have babies with her. IF a vampire wants to have a baby, she is the only person who can carry it. This is a terrible ensemble of female characters. Yes, Arra and Evanna are powerful in their own right but Arra was defeated and killed and Evanna is was literally <i>created</i> just to be a vampire baby-maker! Why are there no good, well-rounded female characters that actually have some purpose to the story?<br /><br /><b>Diversity</b><br /><br />Evanna is a woman who is introduced to the reader. She is strong and powerful but the way her existence is explained is a bit problematic. And there’s honestly not all that much of her in the book to be seen. Other than that, no other diverse characters come to mind. <br /><br /><b>Overall</b><br /><br />If I had to describe <i>Hunters of the Dark</i> with one word, it would probably be “forced”. The plot is forced forward by Mr. Tiny. The writing feels forced. This books just wasn’t enjoyable to me. This is another bridge book and there are already too many in this series for me to be sympathetic towards it. <br /><br /><a href="http://booknoting.tumblr.com/post/116672862350/hunters-of-the-dusk-notes" rel="nofollow noopener">Here is a link to my notes.</a><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15598067620930459636" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_287630748" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/287630748" />
    <a title="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder"><img alt="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572373103p2/3048260.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/287630748?book_show_action=true">Mar 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" href="/user/show/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder">Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780316605960" href="/book/show/1066071.Hunters_of_the_Dusk">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=a-own-book-form">a-own-book-form</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=got-in-2014">got-in-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=part-of-series">part-of-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer287630748" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8791247033398032972"><br/>Nothing like opening a book in a series and finding out it’s skipped forward…by six years. Yes, six years. Hear me sigh in irritation.<br/><br/>The last book left off with a stunning revelation, but we’ve skipped forward now. Once I got past that annoying development, the story continues to demand my attention. <br/><br/>Darren hasn’t seemed to think or tend to the views of the former traitor he was considering before (peace treaties), and while not enjoying killing, does it with more natural ease when it’s needed.</span>
  <span id="freeText8791247033398032972" style="display:none"><br />Nothing like opening a book in a series and finding out it’s skipped forward…by six years. Yes, six years. Hear me sigh in irritation.<br /><br />The last book left off with a stunning revelation, but we’ve skipped forward now. Once I got past that annoying development, the story continues to demand my attention. <br /><br />Darren hasn’t seemed to think or tend to the views of the former traitor he was considering before (peace treaties), and while not enjoying killing, does it with more natural ease when it’s needed. Or else, when he thinks it’s needed. Mr. Tiny has returned and along with his encounter, an interesting sorceress who tells the potentials of the future as well. Characters like Lady Evanna amp up the fantasy aspect.<br /><br />The trio – Darren, Crepsley, and Harkat – leave the mountains finally to begin a classic adventure journey. Fits in well no matter the age level. There are four foretold chances, and the fate of the entire race depends on failure or success. <br /><br />There was also a tossed in other possible outcome that affects Darren more personally, something I hope the next book covers in more detail. It’s dark, it’s serious, and it raises the stakes in a different direction. Curious and revving to go continue this journey in the next book – these just fly by when reading them.<br /><br />Another four star book in the series that works in making this world more complex, more captivating.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8791247033398032972" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1407212487" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1407212487" />
    <a title="Charlotte van den Berg" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23596397-charlotte-van-den-berg"><img alt="Charlotte van den Berg" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1538500164p2/23596397.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1407212487?book_show_action=true">Oct 03, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Charlotte van den Berg" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Charlotte van den Berg" href="/user/show/23596397-charlotte-van-den-berg">Charlotte van den Berg</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23596397-charlotte-van-den-berg?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23596397-charlotte-van-den-berg?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1407212487" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13693612838539644829">When a friend of mine recommended a young adult series to me about vampires I was a little hesitant. Thinking back a few years to the time I tried many vampire series friends of mine loved I almost lost interest completely. But I trusted this friend and decided to check it out. I could always stop reading after the first book. I was relieved to see that this book didn’t look like any of the other vampire books I tried to read so I didn’t have come up with an excuse why I couldn’t read this serie</span>
  <span id="freeText13693612838539644829" style="display:none">When a friend of mine recommended a young adult series to me about vampires I was a little hesitant. Thinking back a few years to the time I tried many vampire series friends of mine loved I almost lost interest completely. But I trusted this friend and decided to check it out. I could always stop reading after the first book. I was relieved to see that this book didn’t look like any of the other vampire books I tried to read so I didn’t have come up with an excuse why I couldn’t read this series. I’m so glad I gave it a chance. <br /><br />This is the seventh book of the series and it still isn’t boring or predictable. These are great books if you feel yourself getting into a reading slump and you need to read a book that’s interesting and easy. I usually read these books when I’m reading a something that’s hard to get through and I need a break.<br /><br />I liked this book but I did have a few problems with some things:<br /><br />This book had a new character I didn’t like. We meet a new prince: Vancha. The way he acts is just too much and extreme. I would have liked him better if the way he behaved was more subtle. There was a conversation between him and Darren where we find out he want to beat the sun so he tortures himself by walking around in daylight. I don’t know maybe I’m wrong but that makes no sense to me.<br /> <br />Darren goes through something called '’the purge’’. It’s a sort of super-fast vampire puberty. I didn’t like this because I loved reading about him struggling with growing up so slowly and it was so unexpected and felt forced. <br /><br />The names vampaneze and vampets. I don’t think it should be very hard to come up with something better than that. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13693612838539644829" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_854585589" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/854585589" />
    <a title="Kat  Hooper" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2177891-kat-hooper"><img alt="Kat  Hooper" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1533675060p2/2177891.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/854585589?book_show_action=true">Feb 14, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kat  Hooper" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kat  Hooper" href="/user/show/2177891-kat-hooper">Kat  Hooper</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2177891-kat-hooper?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer854585589" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3745598306571606878">Originally posted at Fantasy Literature. <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.fantasyliterature.com/reviews/hunters-of-the-dusk/'>http://www.fantasyliterature.com/revi...</a><br/><br/>Hunters of the Dusk is the seventh book in Darren Shan’s CIRQUE DU FREAK series. Though Shan always does a nice job of quickly and sufficiently recapping the plot, it’d be best not to start here. Go back and begin with A Living Nightmare. And be warned that this review will contain spoilers for previous books.<br/><br/>It’s been six years since the events of The Vampire Prince. Young Darren Shan is now one of the leaders of t</span>
  <span id="freeText3745598306571606878" style="display:none">Originally posted at Fantasy Literature. <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.fantasyliterature.com/reviews/hunters-of-the-dusk/">http://www.fantasyliterature.com/revi...</a><br /><br />Hunters of the Dusk is the seventh book in Darren Shan’s CIRQUE DU FREAK series. Though Shan always does a nice job of quickly and sufficiently recapping the plot, it’d be best not to start here. Go back and begin with A Living Nightmare. And be warned that this review will contain spoilers for previous books.<br /><br />It’s been six years since the events of The Vampire Prince. Young Darren Shan is now one of the leaders of the vampires because making him a prince was the only way that the other princes could legally excuse him for failing to pass the trials. Frankly, this part of the plot is disappointing. It’s hard to believe, first, that Darren had to do the trials at all, and second, that the vampire princes can’t manage to change or otherwise get around the ancient rules. And, if making Darren a prince gets him above the law so that he doesn’t have to be executed, why don’t the other princes have the power to make an exception to the law? What’s the point of being a prince if you can’t change or make exceptions to stupid rules? But let’s just pretend we didn’t notice this little problem and move on, shall we?<br /><br />So, anyway, it’s been six years and Darren has been learning all he can about being a prince of the vampires. Then Mr. Tiny shows up and prophesizes that three vampires must hunt down the prince of the vampaneze. They will have four chances to kill him and if they don’t, the vampires will be wiped out and very bad things will happen to the world. The hunters who must go are Darren, Mr. Crepsley, and another who they’ll meet on the way. Harkat, one of the Little People, may accompany them, and they must first go to visit a witch named Lady Evanna. After that, they must follow their hearts rather than actively pursuing the vampaneze prince. Thus, they go back to the Cirque du Freak where Darren reunites with old friends. He also has an encounter with the vampaneze and learns a little more about Mr. Tiny and Mr. Crepsley.<br /><br />Readers who’ve read this far in CIRQUE DU FREAK are unlikely to turn back now and this is another fast moving exciting story. However, it is weakened substantially, in my opinion, by the inclusion of the Prophecy, Destiny, and Fate elements. Darren and company are suddenly no longer self-efficacious. Instead, they are being dragged around by Mr. Tiny’s nebulous ideas of what has to be. We don’t even know what Mr. Tiny is or whose side he’s on. This lends plenty of mystery, but doesn’t make us very confident in Darren’s decision-making process. Unfortunately, this trend continues in the next few books at least. Still, this is unlikely to bother the target audience and the story continues to delight in many ways. I sincerely look forward to finding out what happens to Darren Shan.<br /><br />I continue to read the audio version read by Ralph Lister. As I keep mentioning, he tends to be a little too dramatic with his reading, but I’m used to it now and it doesn’t detract from the story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3745598306571606878" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1292608967" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5467596929650865254">	Darren Shan, now a Vampire of high standing, is sent on a mission along with an Elite Squad to eliminate the threat of the murderous Vampaneze and their Lord. Will Darren succeed, and if he does, will it have been worth it?<br/>	Expanding on the books before it, “ Hunters of the Dusk” might seem like a good book at first. It has action, as well as a fairly interesting plot. However, the problem in the last book has not been fixed. Darren Shan, a mere, young, half-vampire, is chosen by an agent of De</span>
  <span id="freeText5467596929650865254" style="display:none">	Darren Shan, now a Vampire of high standing, is sent on a mission along with an Elite Squad to eliminate the threat of the murderous Vampaneze and their Lord. Will Darren succeed, and if he does, will it have been worth it?<br />	Expanding on the books before it, “ Hunters of the Dusk” might seem like a good book at first. It has action, as well as a fairly interesting plot. However, the problem in the last book has not been fixed. Darren Shan, a mere, young, half-vampire, is chosen by an agent of Destiny to be part of an Elite Squad supposed to eradicate a race of the equivalent of murderous Vampires. I think that this is a bit of a stretch for a series that was about a boy who doesn’t fit in, due to Vampiric powers, but about a boy who doesn’t fit in nonetheless. This book, along with the one after this, were my least favorite in the series. For these reasons, I would give it 3 stars. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5467596929650865254" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText15541313140774784338" style="display:none">Mr. Tiny tells Mr. Crepsley and Darren that they have to go find the Vampaneze Lord and kill him, and that only them and one other vampire that they will find later can kill him. Darren and Mr. Crepsley go to find the other vampire, so they start searching. They find Vancha March, the third vampire. All three of them want to find the Vampaneze Lord, but they don't know where to start, so they just follow their instincts. Then, they do find him, and while trying to kill him, they killed all the Vampaneze except Vancha March's brother, and one other. The one other was the Vampaneze Lord, so it counted as their 1st time, and they only have 4 encounters....<br /><br />Hunters of the Dusk is about Confidence, Not giving up, and Finding the best ways to do things.</span>

I believe he was maybe the brother to Evanna… I'm also pretty sure that the Vampeneze Lord is Steve Leopard/Leonard — since that would make perfect sense! </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1642673849" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15707396484012360998">Darren is now the prince and have quests to do, it is just the beginning. The author made it very fun by adding thoughts, I like reading their thoughts and 'watching' their actions. It's pretty exciting when they are fighting their enemies. Everyone should try this book out, continue with the next book! I can't stop reading the series because their too FUN!!! </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('swtvsb1H8wj9fjGsCt8orfLpohyTV6LbYZsKszLjD+h/2l0SNsMITgKNaU+tKvS9PBKL5CkAd+t4EoWiedDmcw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('EQ5m8prGI13O3XBMwRkephphBYJwODpPsaUxUujjXUvd31RREULYGzEuKK9m7MK21Josespv73+oLL5Do9C00A==')})
  }

Lovecraft (1890-1937), an extremely influential poet and author who mixed science fiction, horror and <\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText12251941923937260018\" style=\"display:none\">What would you get if you mixed Edgar Allan Poe, Alfred Hitchcock and Stephen King? The answer might be something resembling Howard Phillips (H.P.) Lovecraft (1890-1937), an extremely influential poet and author who mixed science fiction, horror and fantasy into a subgenre known as “weird fiction”. Perhaps none encapsulates weird fiction like his creation of the monster Cthulhu, which has been used by other writers to spawn a fictional universe and mythology centered around Cthulhu. Growing up in New England, Lovecraft spun tales that mixed the sleepy history of places like Boston and Providence with legend and magical tales. Though he suffered an untimely death from cancer and wasn’t widely read in his lifetime, his legacy skyrocketed in the subsequent decades, kept alive by outlets like the H.P. Lovecraft Society and the accolades credited to him by the likes of Stephen King, who called him “the 20th century’s greatest practitioner of the classic horror tale.”This edition of Lovecraft’s Ibid is specially formatted with a Table of Contents and is illustrated with over a dozen pictures of Lovecraft, his life and work.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"12251941923937260018\" href=\"#\"   <span id="freeText7991847704368232815" style="display:none">Librarian's note: Also writes books for adults under the name <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7790731.Darren_Dash" rel="nofollow noopener">Darren Dash</a>. And in the past he has released books for adults under the names <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1304819.D_B_Shan" rel="nofollow noopener">D.B. Shan</a> and Darren O'Shaughnessy.<br /><br />Darren Shan (born July 2, 1972 in London, England) is the pen name of the Irish author Darren O'Shaughnessy, as well as the name of the protagonist of his book series The Saga of Darren Shan, also known as The Cirque Du Freak Series in the United States. He is the author of the series The Demonata, The Saga of Larten Crepsley, and Zom-B. He has also released the stand-alone novel, The Thin Executioner, and the stand-alone short novels, Koyasan, and Hagurosan. Plus, for adults, he released The City Trilogy (originally under the name of D.B. Shan), and Lady of the Shades.. </span>
